       <article class="post-65693 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-noise" id="post-65693">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/03/20/test-results-prove-wind-turbine-noise-modelling-faulty/" rel="bookmark">
           Test results prove wind turbine noise modelling faulty
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/03/20/test-results-prove-wind-turbine-noise-modelling-faulty/" rel="bookmark" title="08:04">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2018-03-20T08:04:40+00:00">
            03/20/2018
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/03/20/test-results-prove-wind-turbine-noise-modelling-faulty/#comments">
           4
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p>
          <iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="315" src="https://webapps.9c9media.com/vidi-player/1.4.1/share/iframe.html?currentId=1349797&amp;config=ctvnews/share.json&amp;kruxId=ImoeZsch&amp;cid=%5B%7B%22contentId%22%3A1349797%2C%22ad%22%3A%7B%22adsite%22%3A%22ctv.ctvnews%22%2C%22adzone%22%3A%22embed%22%7D%7D%5D" width="560">
          </iframe>
         </p>
         <p class="x_MsoNormal">
          As a service to Ontarians concerned about the use of suspect noise modelling by engineers working on behalf of wind developers to get projects approved it appears concern is warranted. HCG were instrumental in developing the noise regulations for the Ontario government. Recently they conducted a Section D audit test on the Unifor turbine. Highlights of that test are below;
         </p>
         <div>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Unifor Wind Turbine (Page 2)
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Acoustic Immission Audit January 8, 2018
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Table 1:
           <strong>
            Predicted Sound Levels
           </strong>
           and UTM Coordinates of Selected Locations
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Location Easting Northing Predicted Sound Level
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           [dBA]
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           J Receptor 467256 4919594
           <strong>
            42.7
           </strong>
           ±
           <br/>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           Monitoring Location M1 467348 4919607
           <strong>
            43.9
           </strong>
           *
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           T Receptor 467416 4919124
           <strong>
            40.1
           </strong>
           ±
           <br/>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           Monitoring Location M2 467474 4919119
           <strong>
            39.2
           </strong>
           *
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Q Receptor 467169 4919269
           <strong>
            42.0
           </strong>
           ±
           <br/>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           Monitoring Location M3 467212 4919266
           <strong>
            44.1
           </strong>
           *
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           ± Sound level taken from ENIR [1]. ( Original CAW modelling )  * Sound level predicted by acoustic model created by HGC Engineering.
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           <strong>
            NOTE: 2 of the 3 test locations modelled higher by HCG than by CAW’s original engineering consultant.
           </strong>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Receptor location J is a single storey cottage located at 12 Globe Place. Turbine T1 is
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           approximately 210 m to the southeast. The sound level meter was installed on a fence at the
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           northwest side of the Unifor property, approximately 205 m from T1, designated Monitoring
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           Location M1. The microphone was placed at a height of 4.5 m, consistent with the ENIR.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Table 4a: Monitoring Location M1 – Sound Level Summary
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           10 m Height Wind Speed [m/s]
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           LEQ Sound Level [dBA] 1 2 3 4 m/sec
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p>
           Average Operating (ON) / Std Dev. –
           <br/>
           1 –
           <br/>
           1 47.9 1.5 48.7 1.4
          </p>
          <p>
           Average Ambient (OFF) / Std Dev. 34.4 3.3 36.3 3.2 40.2 2.4 42.8 1.4
          </p>
          <p>
           Wind Project Only – – 47 47
          </p>
          <p>
           Criteria 45 45 45 45 ( our faulty 45 db semi urban classification – normally rural at 40 db )
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Excess – – 2
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           <strong>
            Comment
           </strong>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Closest receptor the Groves home at 12 Gobles Place at 210 m. away from the Unifor turbine was modelled at 42.7 by CAW, predicted at 43.9 by HCG and HCG audit tested it at 47 and 48 dB. An unpublished MOECC approved Section D audit test by CAW engineer on April 27,28,29 2014 had measurements of 45 db at 4m/sec and 57 dB at 6 m/sec. It was later deemed incomplete after found by FOI as CAW called off the test each night as residents unaware of testing being done called in noise complaints.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           The HCG 47 and 48 dB illegal noise levels were based on an alternate test track of less than half the normal amount of measuring supposedly due to lack of good data. We had never heard of this optional test track.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Only low wind speeds between 1 to 4 m/sec (max 14.4km/hr) were used in this reduced data testing track for 1 hour averaging. Meanwhile the MOECC chart shows wind speeds from 4 to 10 m/sec. and shows that all wind speeds from 4 to 8 m/sec shall not exceed the max limit of 45 dB.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Where are the noise test results for wind speeds from 5 to 10 m/sec? No good wind for the 3
           <sup>
            rd
           </sup>
           time?? Common sense says they would be much higher than the 48 dB HCG measured and could most likely be extrapolated by talented acousticians.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           So we have learned that HCG, the architect of Ontario’s noise testing regulations, has just proven how faulty the wind turbine noise modelling scheme is that MOECC uses to approve wind projects in Ontario. And while using low max. wind speeds of 4 m/sec. HCG is off by 5 dB ( 48.7-43.9 ) and that is significant.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Any yet to be approved or built wind projects like those now launching legal challenges based on concern of the adverse effects faulty modelling will have on them appear to be well justified.
          </p>
          <p class="x_gmail-m_-7903376123668433967m_-5514591896170782872m5975073511559323425msoplaintext">
           Greg Schmalz
           <br/>
           <u>
           </u>
           <u>
           </u>
           STOP
          </p>
         </div>

       <article class="post-65620 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-safety category-setbacks category-wind-industry" id="post-65620">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-in-chatham-kent/" rel="bookmark">
           Broken Wind Turbine In Chatham-Kent
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-in-chatham-kent/" rel="bookmark" title="11:58">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2018-01-19T11:58:51+00:00">
            01/19/2018
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-in-chatham-kent/#comments">
           193
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <div class="wp-caption alignright" id="attachment_65621" style="width: 980px">
          <a href="http://blackburnnews.com/chatham/chatham-news/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-chatham-kent/">
           <img alt="" class="size-full wp-image-65621" data-attachment-id="65621" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="wind-turbine-broke-970×400" data-large-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?fit=584%2C241" data-medium-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?fit=300%2C124" data-orig-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?fit=970%2C400" data-orig-size="970,400" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-in-chatham-kent/wind-turbine-broke-970x400/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="241" sizes="(max-width: 584px) 100vw, 584px" src="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=584%2C241" srcset="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=970%2C400 970w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=150%2C62 150w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=300%2C124 300w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=768%2C317 768w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/wind-turbine-broke-970x400.jpg?resize=500%2C206 500w" width="584"/>
          </a>
          <p class="wp-caption-text">
           Photo by Paul Pedro
          </p>
         </div>
         <p>
          <a href="http://blackburnnews.com/chatham/chatham-news/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-chatham-kent/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Blackburn News
          </a>
          <br/>
          Terraform Power crews are investigating after a wind turbine that’s part of a wind energy project just south of Chatham broke in half.
         </p>
         <p>
          The turbine is located at the corner of Drake Rd. and 16 Line.
         </p>
         <p>
          Blackburn News has reached out to the Ministry of Energy and Climate Change, the municipality of Chatham-Kent, and officials with Terraform Power for more details.
         </p>
         <p>
          Chatham-Kent’s fire chief is at the scene and says it is currently disconnected from the power grid.
         </p>
         <p>
          Workers are currently putting up safety fencing around the broken turbine and Chatham-Kent police are also stationed there.
          <a href="http://blackburnnews.com/chatham/chatham-news/2018/01/19/broken-wind-turbine-chatham-kent/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>

            <div class="tiled-gallery-item" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject">
             <a border="0" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2010/04/29/queens-park-protest-pictures-2/vow/" itemprop="url">
              <meta content="190" itemprop="width"/>
              <meta content="190" itemprop="height"/>
              <img alt="VoW" data-attachment-id="10914" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"3.6","credit":"","camera":"FinePix S1500","caption":"","created_timestamp":"1272454132","copyright":"","focal_length":"33.4","iso":"64","shutter_speed":"0.00238095238095","title":""}' data-image-title="VoW" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/vow.jpg?fit=584%2C438" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/vow.jpg?fit=300%2C225" data-orig-file="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/vow.jpg" data-orig-size="1024,768" data-original-height="190" data-original-width="190" height="190" itemprop="http://schema.org/image" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/vow.jpg?w=190&amp;h=190&amp;crop=1" style="width: 190px; height: 190px;" title="VoW" width="190"/>
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-group" data-original-height="194" data-original-width="194" style="width: 194px; height: 194px;">
            <div class="tiled-gallery-item" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject">
             <a border="0" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2013/05/19/unhealthy-setback/stephana/" itemprop="url">
              <meta content="190" itemprop="width"/>
              <meta content="190" itemprop="height"/>
              <img alt="Stephana" data-attachment-id="55677" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="Stephana" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/stephana.jpg?fit=500%2C975" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/stephana.jpg?fit=153%2C300" data-orig-file="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/stephana.jpg" data-orig-size="500,975" data-original-height="190" data-original-width="190" height="190" itemprop="http://schema.org/image" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/stephana.jpg?w=190&amp;h=190&amp;crop=1" style="width: 190px; height: 190px;" title="Stephana" width="190"/>
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p>
          Stephana Johnston, the grandmother of our wind resistance, has passed away at age 88. Somehow I still think she will post a comment here about that, she seems that eternal.
         </p>
         <p>
          I said she was the ‘grandmother,’ though in the way that spoke to her intellect, her thoughtfulness, courage and determination. We watched her lead this last fight while she was well into her 80’s – how many of us can even dream of accomplishing what she did, at that age, while evicted from her home and suffering debilitating health effects from the wind turbines that surrounded her? Do a search for her name on this site and the results are endless. She was at nearly every ERT hearing – not just in the audience, but participating, which means she had to prepare for each of the appeals as well!  In-between, she was at as many protests as I can even remember. Even if it was in downtown Toronto. Did someone drive her? Nope, she could do it herself.
         </p>
         <p>
          I have so many fond memories of her, every time she arrived our spirits were lifted. Some were humorous as she had a wry wit, many were touching, but most were teaching moments. You couldn’t help but watch her deliberate movements, and listen to her well chosen words, and know that everything she did and said had meaning and purpose. When we were banned from handing out papers at a Pembina meeting on wind turbines, she turned her walker around and sat there by the entrance door, continuing to hand those banished papers to attendees. I remember glancing at the police officer, noting he wouldn’t touch her, and she knew it – because she was in the right. She was the perfect quiet protestor.
         </p>
         <p>
          I know many of you will have memories as well – do share them – she’d enjoy it so much.
         </p>
         <p>
          Here are some bits from the archives that describe her personality, her struggle and work over the years:
         </p>
         <hr/>
         <p>
          <strong>
           <a href="https://mlwindaction.org/2012/10/04/fisherville-ert-in-the-land-of-all-day-breakfast/#more-3928" rel="noopener" style="text-decoration: underline;" target="_blank">
            Fisherville ERT: In the Land of All Day Breakfast
           </a>
           <br/>
          </strong>
          … Mr. Adamson (Ministry of Environment Lawyer) chafed at the very idea of the individual post-turbine witness testimony saying that,”…they (post-turbine witnesses) should not be allowed to testify about their medical issues.”
         </p>
         <p>
          The arguments reflect an “archaic-modernist” view that the peasants are in the way – they don’t deserve even the semblance of judicial fairness if they cannot afford the demands put upon them. Clear Creek resident, and witness, Stephana Johnston was seated beside me. A tear came to her eye when he said this.
         </p>
         <hr/>
         <p>
          <strong>
           <a href="https://mlwindaction.org/2012/05/05/haldimand-appeal-may-4th/#more-3452" rel="noopener" style="text-decoration: underline;" target="_blank">
            Haldimand Appeal – May 4th
            <br/>
           </a>
          </strong>
          <strong>
           …
          </strong>
          NextEra was of much the same mind, though counsel John Terry, took a bit less time to spew the same blather and nonsense. He took pains to explain that he must have the extensive medical records so that he may have them competently reviewed and so “test” the case evidence for verity. Why he needs 10 years worth of records was not explained, nor did Ms. Harris offer any rationale either.
         </p>
         <p>
          There were a couple of questions from the ERT panel members. One asked Mr.Terry how he would view the call for extensive evidence if this case is viewed as a “public interest” case. Mr. Terry replied that in the interests of fairness to defendants, a “robust process” is needed with appropriate expert testimony.
         </p>
         <p>
          Another question to him was: Is a family doctor’s opinion (diagnosis) sufficient (evidence). Mr. Terry said that the G.P.’s notes need expert evaluation. Stephana Johnson turned to me and softly said, “There are no doctors expert in this medical problem.” – that from someone who can offer expert (though unofficial) opinion.
          <a class="more-link" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2018/01/11/stephana-johnston-ontario-wind-resistances-grandmother/#more-65599">
           Continue reading
           <span class="meta-nav">
            →
           </span>
          </a>
         </p>

       <article class="post-65547 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-ontario-government category-wind-industry" id="post-65547">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/12/27/massive-300mw-wind-project-planned-south-of-sudbury-largest-wind-project-in-ontario-tallest-turbines/" rel="bookmark">
           Largest wind project in Ontario, with tallest turbines, going up beside French River Provincial Park
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/12/27/massive-300mw-wind-project-planned-south-of-sudbury-largest-wind-project-in-ontario-tallest-turbines/" rel="bookmark" title="15:46">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-12-27T15:46:13+00:00">
            12/27/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/12/27/massive-300mw-wind-project-planned-south-of-sudbury-largest-wind-project-in-ontario-tallest-turbines/#comments">
           18
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           <a href="http://henveyinletwind.com/documents/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
            Henvey Inlet Wind
           </a>
           will use
           <strong>
            87 Vestas 3.45 MW turbines
           </strong>
           right beside
           <a href="https://www.ontarioparks.com/park/frenchriver" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
            <strong>
             The French River Provincial Park
            </strong>
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          <a href="https://www.ontarioparks.com/park/frenchriver">
           <img alt="" class="alignright wp-image-65554 size-large" data-attachment-id="65554" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="frenchriver" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?fit=584%2C171" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?fit=300%2C88" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?fit=1200%2C350" data-orig-size="1200,350" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/12/27/massive-300mw-wind-project-planned-south-of-sudbury-largest-wind-project-in-ontario-tallest-turbines/frenchriver/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="171" sizes="(max-width: 584px) 100vw, 584px" src="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=584%2C171" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=1024%2C299 1024w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=150%2C44 150w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=300%2C88 300w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=768%2C224 768w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?resize=500%2C146 500w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/frenchriver.jpg?w=1200 1200w" width="584"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="alignright wp-image-65549 size-large" data-attachment-id="65549" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"1"}' data-image-title="henveyinletsudbury" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?fit=584%2C391" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?fit=300%2C201" data-orig-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?fit=1078%2C721" data-orig-size="1078,721" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/12/27/massive-300mw-wind-project-planned-south-of-sudbury-largest-wind-project-in-ontario-tallest-turbines/henveyinletsudbury/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="391" sizes="(max-width: 584px) 100vw, 584px" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=584%2C391" srcset="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=1024%2C685 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=150%2C100 150w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=300%2C201 300w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=768%2C514 768w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?resize=449%2C300 449w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/12/henveyinletsudbury.jpg?w=1078 1078w" width="584"/>
          </a>
          <a href="http://www.thesudburystar.com/2017/12/26/landmark-wind-farm-in-works-for-henvey-inlet" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           The Sudbury Star
          </a>
          <br/>
          An international energy company has secured $1 billion in financing to build the largest wind project in Ontario on a reserve south of Sudbury.
         </p>
         <p>
          Pattern Development revealed plans Tuesday to construct a 300-megawatt wind project located on Henvey Inlet First Nation Reserve No. 2 on the northeast shore of the Georgian Bay.
         </p>
         <p>
          Pattern Development and Nigig Power Corporation, a wholly owned subsidiary of Henvey Inlet First Nation, are joint venture partners in the project.
         </p>
         <p>
          “This landmark project is a first on many fronts: largest wind project in Ontario, largest on-reserve wind installation in Canada, highest hub heights in North America, and the first to develop a First Nation Environmental Stewardship Regime under the First Nations Lands Management Act,” Mike Garland, CEO of Pattern Development, said in a release.
         </p>
         <p>
          “We are proud to be partners with Henvey Inlet First Nation. Together we’re excited to kick off construction on this historic project that will harness the strong and steady winds blowing across the Georgian Bay to create hundreds of local jobs and provide a significant new source of revenue for Henvey Inlet First Nation.”
          <a href="http://www.thesudburystar.com/2017/12/26/landmark-wind-farm-in-works-for-henvey-inlet" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>

       <!-- #post-65525 -->
       <article class="post-65517 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-bats-and-birds" id="post-65517">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/27/researchers-study-impact-of-turbines-on-golden-eagles/" rel="bookmark">
           Researchers study impact of turbines on golden eagles
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/27/researchers-study-impact-of-turbines-on-golden-eagles/" rel="bookmark" title="08:00">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-11-27T08:00:57+00:00">
            11/27/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/27/researchers-study-impact-of-turbines-on-golden-eagles/#comments">
           5
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p class="speakable-p-1 p-text">
          <a href="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="alignright size-medium wp-image-5260" data-attachment-id="5260" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="golden-eagle-altamont-400×300" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?fit=400%2C300" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?fit=300%2C225" data-orig-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?fit=400%2C300" data-orig-size="400,300" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2009/09/09/windmills-are-killing-our-birds/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="225" sizes="(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?resize=300%2C225" srcset="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?resize=300%2C225 300w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?resize=150%2C112 150w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/09/golden-eagle-altamont-400x300.jpg?resize=400%2C300 400w" width="300"/>
          </a>
          Ximena Tapia,
          <a href="http://www.lcsun-news.com/story/news/education/nmsu/2017/11/25/researchers-study-impact-turbines-golden-eagles/894837001/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Sun-News
          </a>
          <br/>
          A New Mexico State University professor in the College of Agricultural, Consumer and Environmental Sciences is conducting research on golden eagles being killed by wind turbines and other human-related factors.
         </p>
         <p class="speakable-p-2 p-text">
          Gary Roemer, professor for the Department of Fish, Wildlife and Conservation Ecology, is conducting a research project to identify whether certain factors impact golden eagle populations. Some of the factors that impact the eagles are electrocutions, vehicle strikes and illegal shootings, but another more recent factor is wind turbine strikes, Roemer said.
         </p>
         <p class="p-text">
          From 1997 to 2012, there were 85 eagle fatalities reported in 32 facilities around the United States. More than 78 percent of those fatalities occurred from 2008 to 2012. Roemer said there is no way to know exactly how many eagles are killed, “as monitoring programs are usually not in place at wind energy facilities.”
         </p>
         <p class="p-text">
          His research is focused on finding out where the eagles that have been killed come from. Roemer said eagles “breed throughout the Western U.S., Alaska and throughout portions of Canada, but they can move a lot.” Many eagles from northern portions of the continent, such as Alaska and Canada, migrate to southern locales in the winter, including New Mexico and Texas.
         </p>
         <p class="p-text">
          According to the American Wind Energy Association, there are 863 wind turbines in New Mexico, generating enough clean electricity to power about 334,000 homes. During 2016, wind energy provided 10.95 percent of all in-state electricity production. Although wind energy has many environmental benefits, it also has the potential to impact eagles and other wildlife.
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p class="p-text">
           “If you put a wind farm down here in New Mexico, you might not only be whacking New Mexico breeding birds, but you might be whacking birds that are breeding in Alaska or the Canadian Arctic,” Roemer said.
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p class="p-text">
          In January 2017, under the Obama administration, a rule was implemented that allows wind-energy companies to accidentally kill or injure eagles while operating high-speed turbines for up to 30 years. That is six times longer than the former rule, which was five years. The rule change also increased the number of eagles the companies can be permitted to accidentally kill or injure, but only under certain conditions.
          <a href="http://www.lcsun-news.com/story/news/education/nmsu/2017/11/25/researchers-study-impact-turbines-golden-eagles/894837001/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">
          <div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social sd-social-icon sd-sharing">
           <h3 class="sd-title">
            Share this:
           </h3>
           <div class="sd-content">
            <ul>
             <li class="share-email">
              <a class="share-email sd-button share-icon no-text" data-shared="" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/27/researchers-study-impact-of-turbines-on-golden-eagles/?share=email" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" title="Click to email this to a friend">
               <span>
               </span>
               <span class="sharing-screen-reader-text">
                Click to email this to a friend (Opens in new window)
               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li class="share-print">
              <a class="share-print sd-button share-icon no-text" data-shared="" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/27/researchers-study-impact-of-turbines-on-golden-eagles/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" title="Click to print">
               <span>

       <!-- #post-65517 -->
       <article class="post-65491 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-ethics category-legal category-wind-industry" id="post-65491">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/08/couple-ordered-to-pay-wpd-costs-in-turbine-appeal-despite-concern-for-citizens-who-try-to-challenge-government/" rel="bookmark">
           Couple ordered to pay wpd costs in turbine appeal – despite concern for citizens who try to challenge government
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/08/couple-ordered-to-pay-wpd-costs-in-turbine-appeal-despite-concern-for-citizens-who-try-to-challenge-government/" rel="bookmark" title="08:10">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-11-08T08:10:43+00:00">
            11/08/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/11/08/couple-ordered-to-pay-wpd-costs-in-turbine-appeal-despite-concern-for-citizens-who-try-to-challenge-government/#comments">
           14
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <div class="wp-caption alignright" id="attachment_4833" style="width: 310px">
          <a href="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif">
           <img alt="" class="size-medium wp-image-4833" data-attachment-id="4833" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="4156" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?fit=475%2C380" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?fit=300%2C240" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?fit=475%2C380" data-orig-size="475,380" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2009/08/23/farmers-flee-as-turbines-trigger-despair/attachment/4156/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="240" sizes="(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px" src="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?resize=300%2C240" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?resize=300%2C240 300w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/4156.gif?resize=150%2C120 150w" width="300"/>
          </a>
          <p class="wp-caption-text">
           Art by Paul Bloomer, The Money Counter
          </p>
         </div>
         <p>
          <a href="http://www.countylive.ca/couple-ordered-to-pay-wpd-costs-in-turbine-appeal-despite-concern-for-citizens-who-try-to-challenge-government/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           CountyLive
          </a>
          <br/>
          Two County residents have been ordered to pay wpd Canada $75,000 in costs in the loss of their appeal of a judicial review decision they had hoped would deny industrial wind turbines due to cultural heritage impacts.
         </p>
         <p>
          South Marysburgh residents Liz Driver and Edwin Rowse challenged the approval of the turbines based on the adequacy of consideration given to heritage resources in the hamlet. They also have property that will be affected by turbines.
         </p>
         <p>
          The judicial review was heard in April at Osgoode Hall. They were informed, in June, that they lost their case.
         </p>
         <p>
          “The decision, in our view, did not show that the court had considered all the evidence and the arguments were not well founded; therefore, we brought a motion for leave to appeal the decision,” said Driver.
         </p>
         <p>
          One of three judges responsible for the appeal decision Oct. 24, 2017 did not agree with the awarding of costs and stated concern for citizens who want to challenge the government in court.
         </p>
         <p>
          “My difficulty is with a concern for public participation,” said J. Lederer in dissention of the costs. “As a matter of social policy we want people to engage with government when they are unhappy with, or seek clarification of, decisions that have been made. We detract from that ambition if we too easily tell people they will have to pay costs if they engage, but do not succeed, particularly in amounts as high as $75,000.”
         </p>
         <p>
          Lederer stated wpd Canada was in some sense a bystander to the main debate in the case.
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           “The primary submissions in response to the applicants were made on behalf of the Director (Ministry of Environment and Climate Change). It was with this party that the principal defence of the process rested.”
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          The Director (MOECC) did not seek costs.
         </p>
         <p>
          “The concern of the corporation is a commercial concern,” Lederer stated. “To my mind, those who seek approvals to construct and operate projects that, by their nature, will be controversial, have to expect that those who are impacted will seek to express their concern… As I see it, companies wanting to undertake these projects have to be prepared, when the circumstances call for it, to accept this as a cost of obtaining the required approvals, in the vernacular, as a cost of doing business.”
          <a href="http://www.countylive.ca/couple-ordered-to-pay-wpd-costs-in-turbine-appeal-despite-concern-for-citizens-who-try-to-challenge-government/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">
          <div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social sd-social-icon sd-sharing">

       <!-- #post-65491 -->
       <article class="post-65477 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-bats-and-birds category-environmental category-ethics category-fish-and-wildlife category-green-energy-act category-health category-human-rights-2 category-ontario-government category-safety category-wind-industry" id="post-65477">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/10/08/ontario-gothic/" rel="bookmark">
           Ontario Gothic
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/10/08/ontario-gothic/" rel="bookmark" title="10:56">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-10-08T10:56:53+00:00">
            10/08/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/10/08/ontario-gothic/#comments">
           42
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p>
          <a href="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="alignright size-medium wp-image-65479" data-attachment-id="65479" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"1"}' data-image-title="OntarioGothic" data-large-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?fit=584%2C704" data-medium-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?fit=249%2C300" data-orig-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?fit=1200%2C1448" data-orig-size="1200,1448" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/10/08/ontario-gothic/ontariogothic-2/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="300" sizes="(max-width: 249px) 100vw, 249px" src="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?resize=249%2C300" srcset="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?resize=249%2C300 249w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?resize=124%2C150 124w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?resize=768%2C927 768w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?resize=849%2C1024 849w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/OntarioGothic-1.jpg?w=1200 1200w" width="249"/>
          </a>
          <a href="http://wellingtontimes.ca/ontario-gothic/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Wellington Times
          </a>
          , Rick Conroy
          <br/>
          Mary Shelley is said to have conceived the story of
          <em>
           Frankenstein,
          </em>
          a manmade monster let loose upon the countryside, while under the influence of opium in the cold summer of 1816. The gothic horror story, it turns out, was the work of a dark imagination fuelled by opioids.
         </p>
         <p>
          It begs the question: what was Kathleen Wynne and her government smoking when they let loose their own man-made monsters across rural Ontario—in the form of industrial wind developers and speculators?
         </p>
         <p>
          Even if you buy the sentiment that their motivations were well-intentioned, the undeniable outcome of the
          <em>
           Green Energy Act
          </em>
          is that Kathleen Wynne and Dalton McGuinty have spawned armies of amoral monstrous corporate creatures and have let them loose to roam unfettered across the province. To wreak havoc in rural communities. To despoil the environment. To slaughter endangered species. To make folks sick.
         </p>
         <p>
          Worse, our government has paved the way, clearing hurdles and slashing regulations to enable these creatures to prey upon vulnerable communities, natural habitats and endangered species. Now they have lost control of their grotesque creations. Even Kathleen Wynne must know how this story ends.
         </p>
         <p>
          Near Chatham, folks believe the wind developer working nearby has poisoned their wells—allowing toxins into their drinking supply. They have done the testing. They have spoken out. They have protested. Marched on Queen’s Park. Kathleen Wynne has ignored them.
         </p>
         <p>
          Wynne, her government and her supporters comfort themselves believing the scourge they have unleashed—though ugly and abusive— is a necessary evil. That the greater good is being served. They ignore the folks holding up jars of black liquid, pleading with the province to test their water, drawn from wells that have become undrinkable since the wind developer began driving piles into the bedrock to secure its massive wind turbines. Even Chatham- Kent’s mayor has demanded Kathleen Wynne intervene to protect these residents. It has made no difference.
         </p>
         <p>
          Left without the protection of the province—without the safeguards that would protect them from any other development— these folks took matters into their own hands. In August, they began blockading the construction site— neighbours joining together to form a line against the threat to their drinking water.
         </p>
         <p>
          On Monday, in a cruel blow, the developers— a Korean conglomerate and its American partner—won a court injunction barring any further blockades of the project. The judge said he wasn’t trying to muzzle opponents, but to “prohibit unlawful acts”.
         </p>
         <p>
          In Ontario’s perverse hunger for industrial wind turbines, it turns out Chatham-Kent residents must first prove they have been poisoned by the developer, before they may seek justice. By then, of course, the damage will have been done. Recourse will expensive and, for most, unattainable.
         </p>
         <p>
          Four years ago, the giant American wind developer Next Era sued Esther Wrightman for defamation. On her website she had altered the company’s logo to NextError and Next Terror. They wanted the logos removed or they would litigate the mother of two young children into oblivion. All these years later, the legal action is still pending. Wrightman wakes up every morning with the weight of this action still weighing on her head.
          <a href="http://wellingtontimes.ca/ontario-gothic/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">

       <article class="post-65441 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-owr" id="post-65441">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/wpd-canada-turns-off-wind-turbine-project/" rel="bookmark">
           WPD Canada turns off wind turbine project
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/wpd-canada-turns-off-wind-turbine-project/" rel="bookmark" title="08:56">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-09-28T08:56:08+00:00">
            09/28/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/wpd-canada-turns-off-wind-turbine-project/#comments">
           9
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <h1>
          <a href="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="size-full wp-image-47256 alignright" data-attachment-id="47256" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="Clearview" data-large-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?fit=195%2C138" data-medium-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?fit=195%2C138" data-orig-file="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?fit=195%2C138" data-orig-size="195,138" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2012/08/10/comprehensive-report-from-clearview/clearview-2/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="138" sizes="(max-width: 195px) 100vw, 195px" src="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?resize=195%2C138" srcset="https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?w=195 195w, https://i0.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/clearview.jpg?resize=150%2C106 150w" width="195"/>
          </a>
          Congrats to all who fought and WON!
         </h1>
         <p>
          <a href="http://www.bayshorebroadcasting.ca/news_item.php?NewsID=96028" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Bayshore Broadcasting
          </a>
          , Kevin Bernard
          <br/>
          A BIG WIN for opponents of Giant wind turbines in Ontario.
         </p>
         <p>
          The appeal period has run out, and WPD Canada has decided it will NOT proceed with the Fairview Wind Project in Clearview township.
         </p>
         <p>
          Last month, approval for the wind turbines was revoked, but the company had until September 16th to file an appeal.
         </p>
         <p>
          The Environmental Review Tribunal revoked the previous Renewable Energy Approval, saying WPD Canada’s plans for 8 turbines just outside Stayner would pose serious harm to human health with the turbines in the flight path of two nearby airports.
         </p>
         <p>
          When the ERT ruling came down in mid-August, Opponent Betty Schneider didn’t believe the company would go quietly into the night, so she wasn’t celebrating at that point.
         </p>
         <p>
          Now, Schneider says she would like to fill up her old swimming pool with champagne and celebrate.
         </p>
         <p>
          Schneider says she is numb, that the battle is finally over.
         </p>
         <p>
          WPD Canada has been working on the plan for wind turbines in Clearview for roughly a decade.
         </p>
         <p>
          Manager of Communications for WPD Canada, Kevin Surette tells Bayshore Broadcasting news in an email September 18th that the Board of Directors has decided not to proceed with the Fairview Project.
         </p>
         <p>
          He declined to make any further comments.
         </p>
         <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">
          <div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social sd-social-icon sd-sharing">

       <!-- #post-65441 -->
       <article class="post-65434 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-environmental category-ethics category-green-energy-act category-health category-ontario-government category-wind-industry" id="post-65434">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/thirteenth-complaint-filed-against-wind-turbine-project-for-water-well-interference-in-c-k/" rel="bookmark">
           Thirteenth complaint filed against wind turbine project for water well interference in C-K
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/thirteenth-complaint-filed-against-wind-turbine-project-for-water-well-interference-in-c-k/" rel="bookmark" title="08:43">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-09-28T08:43:41+00:00">
            09/28/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/09/28/thirteenth-complaint-filed-against-wind-turbine-project-for-water-well-interference-in-c-k/#comments">
           10
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p>
          <a href="https://canadians.org/media/thirteenth-complaint-filed-against-samsung-wind-turbine-project-water-well-interference#.WcxBfGTfQcA.twitter" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Council of Canadians
          </a>
          <br/>
          September 27, 2017
          <br/>
          Chatham, ON – Thirteen Chatham area well owners have now filed water well interference complaints following the start of construction on a 34 turbine wind power project near their farms. The Council of Canadians is demanding work stop on the project immediately.
         </p>
         <p>
          The project developer, North Kent Wind One (owned by Samsung Energy and Pattern Energy), started pile driving for the first turbine foundation in late June. The vibrations caused by the pile driving can be felt hundreds of meters away. Before construction began, experts predicted that local wells could suffer siltation problems from the vibrations. Some of the 13 wells affected to date have become so silted up that water no longer flows through the household plumbing.
         </p>
         <p>
          Chatham-Kent residents have been working to protect their well water after learning of pollution problems faced by dozens of families in neighbouring Dover Township where wells began showing high levels of black silt as soon as pile driving started for various wind turbine projects built there over the last eight years. Both counties sit atop the Kettle Point black shale bedrock formation.
          <a href="https://canadians.org/media/thirteenth-complaint-filed-against-samsung-wind-turbine-project-water-well-interference#.WcxBfGTfQcA.twitter" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read more
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
         </p>
         <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en">
          <p dir="ltr" lang="en">
           13 wells destroyed now.
           <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/waterislife?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">
            #waterislife
           </a>
           <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/waterwellsfirst?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">
            #waterwellsfirst
           </a>
           <a href="https://t.co/IloenlL7Lc">
            pic.twitter.com/IloenlL7Lc
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           — Water Wells First! (@WaterWellsFirst)
           <a href="https://twitter.com/WaterWellsFirst/status/913213514432630789?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">
            September 28, 2017
           </a>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          <script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js">
          </script>
         </p>
         <p>
         </p>
         <p>
          Meanwhile C-K Medical Officer of Health Dr. Colby just encouraged  everyone to trust his doctor status and continue filtering out the “crud”. Or… drill a new well, like he’s had to.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="https://chathamvoice.com/2017/09/27/well-concerns-not-appeased/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           The Chatham Voice
          </a>
          <br/>
          “Nobody wants to drink dirty water that looks like chocolate milk; I get that.
          <strong>
           But if you filter that crud out of there,
          </strong>
          is there any evidence there is an increased solution of toxins in that water that could pose a health problem, and the answer is no,” Colby said, noting no evidence has come across his desk. “If you’re more interested in your convictions than the facts that I’m trying to give you, we’re not going to get an agreement on this issue.”
         </p>
         <p>
          Colby said he has a well and had sediment problems, and ended up drilling a new well. When asked how many turbines are nearby, he said he could count 47.
          <a href="https://chathamvoice.com/2017/09/27/well-concerns-not-appeased/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>
         <hr/>
         <p>
          From the archives, in case you think this has gone on way too long with no action from our government:
         </p>
         <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en">
          <p dir="ltr" lang="en">

           </a>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>

         </p>

       <article class="post-65400 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-environmental category-health category-ministry-of-the-environment-ontario category-municipalities-of-ontario category-wind-industry" id="post-65400">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/08/31/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site/" rel="bookmark">
           Frustrated Chatham-Kent residents stage blockade at wind turbine site
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/08/31/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site/" rel="bookmark" title="19:42">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-08-31T19:42:35+00:00">
            08/31/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">

        <div class="entry-content">
         <p>

           <img alt="" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-65401" data-attachment-id="65401" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"0"}' data-image-title="DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?fit=584%2C389" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?fit=300%2C200" data-orig-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?fit=1200%2C799" data-orig-size="1200,799" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/08/31/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site/diaecygvoaan7pk/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="389" sizes="(max-width: 584px) 100vw, 584px" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=584%2C389" srcset="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=1024%2C682 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=150%2C100 150w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=300%2C200 300w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=768%2C511 768w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?resize=451%2C300 451w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/DIaEcYgVoAAn7pK.jpg?w=1200 1200w" width="584"/>
          </a>
          <a href="http://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/windsor/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site-1.4266462" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           CBC News
          </a>
          <br/>
          Chatham-Kent residents frustrated with wind turbine construction they blame for tainting their drinking water staged another blockade Tuesday morning and have temporarily shut down the North Kent Wind project.
         </p>
         <p>
          It is the second blockade in as many weeks by the group calling itself Water Wells First. It is protesting what it believes is provincial inaction on pile driving residents claim is pushing bits of sediment into their drinking water.
         </p>
         <p>
          “The people here in the community just feel like they’re sitting like guinea pigs, waiting to be plucked out and experimented on,” said spokesperson Kevin Jakubec during the blockade held on Aug. 17.  “The tensions are boiling over here.”
         </p>
         <p>
          “The people here in the community just feel like they’re sitting like guinea pigs, waiting to be plucked out and experimented on,” said spokesperson Kevin Jakubec during the blockade held on Aug. 17.
          <br/>
          “The tensions are boiling over here.”
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="size-full wp-image-65402 alignright" data-attachment-id="65402" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":"","orientation":"1"}' data-image-title="" data-large-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?fit=338%2C450" data-medium-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?fit=225%2C300" data-orig-file="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?fit=338%2C450" data-orig-size="338,450" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/08/31/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site/canwea-municipal-world-2011-2/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="450" sizes="(max-width: 338px) 100vw, 338px" src="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?resize=338%2C450" srcset="https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?w=338 338w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?resize=113%2C150 113w, https://i1.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/08/canwea-municipal-world-2011.jpg?resize=225%2C300 225w" width="338"/>
          </a>
          Following that blockade, Chatham-Kent Mayor Randy Hope wrote to minister of environment Chris Ballard, asking for an “immediate intervention” in the water quality issues due to “conflicting reports” on water quality that created “fear and concern among residents.”
         </p>
         <p>
          “The ministry cannot remain silent on this very important issue,” the mayor added. “This is an extremely urgent matter which demands immediate, decisive action from your ministry and government.”
          <a href="http://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/windsor/frustrated-chatham-kent-residents-stage-blockade-at-wind-turbine-site-1.4266462" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>

       <article class="post-65369 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-investment category-jobs category-ontario-government category-subsidies-costs category-viability category-wind-industry" id="post-65369">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/07/19/wind-subsidies-gone-samsung-gone/" rel="bookmark">
           Wind subsidies gone, Samsung gone
          </a>
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="sep">
           Posted on
          </span>
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/07/19/wind-subsidies-gone-samsung-gone/" rel="bookmark" title="10:42">
           <time class="entry-date" datetime="2017-07-19T10:42:15+00:00">
            07/19/2017
           </time>
          </a>
          <span class="by-author">
           <span class="sep">
            by
           </span>
           <span class="author vcard">
            <a class="url fn n" href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/author/windaction/" rel="author" title="View all posts by wind resist">
             wind resist
            </a>
           </span>
          </span>
         </div>
         <!-- .entry-meta -->
         <div class="comments-link">
          <a href="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2017/07/19/wind-subsidies-gone-samsung-gone/#comments">
           30
          </a>
         </div>
        </header>
        <!-- .entry-header -->
        <div class="entry-content">
         <p>
          <a href="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg">
           <img alt="" class="alignright size-full wp-image-60311" data-attachment-id="60311" data-comments-opened="1" data-image-description="" data-image-meta='{"aperture":"0","credit":"","camera":"","caption":"","created_timestamp":"0","copyright":"","focal_length":"0","iso":"0","shutter_speed":"0","title":""}' data-image-title="South Kent Wind Samsung Pattern Chatham Kent New Scotland Line" data-large-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?fit=584%2C412" data-medium-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?fit=300%2C211" data-orig-file="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?fit=1024%2C723" data-orig-size="1024,723" data-permalink="http://ontario-wind-resistance.org/2014/02/15/south-kent-wind-turbine-destruction/south-kent-wind-samsung-pattern-chatham-kent-new-scotland-line-2/" data-recalc-dims="1" height="412" sizes="(max-width: 584px) 100vw, 584px" src="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?resize=584%2C412" srcset="https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?w=1024 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?resize=150%2C105 150w, https://i2.wp.com/ontario-wind-resistance.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/South-Kent-Wind-Samsung-Pattern-Chatham-Kent-New-Scotland-Line1.jpg?resize=300%2C211 300w" width="584"/>
          </a>
          <a href="http://www.torontosun.com/2017/07/18/ontario-wind-turbine-factory-closing-hundreds-losing-jobs" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Toronto Sun
          </a>
          , Jennifer Bieman and Megan Stacey
          <br/>
          The loss of 340 jobs at a factory that makes blades for wind turbines could be harbinger of troubles ahead in Ontario’s green-energy industry, a leading analyst says.
         </p>
         <p>
          Siemens Canada announced Tuesday it’s closing its Tillsonburg plant, one of four Ontario green-energy factories set up under a controversial, multi-billion-dollar deal with Korean industrial giant Samsung.
         </p>
         <p>
          The closing of one of the town’s largest employers came after weeks of nervous speculation.
         </p>
         <p>
          But energy analyst Tom Adams said Ontario’s green-energy industry could be in for a rough ride if it doesn’t lay its hands on orders from outside Ontario, arguing the provincial market is saturated with wind and solar electricity brought online since the Liberal government plunged headlong into green energy in 2009.
         </p>
         <p>
          “I think it was always pretty obvious that whatever jobs were going to arise from the Green Energy Act were all temporary or almost all temporary,” Adams said, referencing the provincial law that paved the way for big wind farms in Ontario under contracts paying energy giants more than consumers pay for power.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           “Samsung had no history in renewable energy before they came to Ontario. They came only for the subsidies, and when the subsidies dry up, they’ll disappear as quick as they landed,”
          </strong>
          said Adams, an independent energy and environmental advisor and researcher.
          <a href="http://www.torontosun.com/2017/07/18/ontario-wind-turbine-factory-closing-hundreds-losing-jobs" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
           Read article
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="sharedaddy sd-sharing-enabled">
          <div class="robots-nocontent sd-block sd-social sd-social-icon sd-sharing">
